<div id="review_158910811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158910811" />
    <a title="Hanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5045436-hanna"><img alt="Hanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521519098p2/5045436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158910811?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hanna" href="/user/show/5045436-hanna">Hanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158910811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16668112195042396671">While the book is quite disturbing, it’s an eye-opener at the same time. It gyrates on the woeful life of Daelyn Rice who at a very young age got bullied inexorably. Due to a failed suicide attempt, she became incapacitated to speak. The stigmas poisoned her: the way she reasons out seems irrational sometimes. The way she treats people seems like a simulacrum that she’s a bully herself. At least, that’s what I think.<br/><br/>While reading the book, I felt like I bought myself a manual in committing suici</span>
  <span id="freeText16668112195042396671" style="display:none">While the book is quite disturbing, it’s an eye-opener at the same time. It gyrates on the woeful life of Daelyn Rice who at a very young age got bullied inexorably. Due to a failed suicide attempt, she became incapacitated to speak. The stigmas poisoned her: the way she reasons out seems irrational sometimes. The way she treats people seems like a simulacrum that she’s a bully herself. At least, that’s what I think.<br /><br />While reading the book, I felt like I bought myself a manual in committing suicide. Why, it contains ‘practical’ tips to kill yourself. Exsanguination startled me, by the way. Inspite of all the pep talks and blandishments, she remained unperturbed that for the last time, she will do it. Perfect and smooth. With the help of through-the-light.com, a website she one day came across, she started regaling her story to other j_does across the globe who had their share of being bullied as well. It’s a heartbreaking book at its core. It emanates one facet of reality; our words can really kill. We may or may not notice it but the words we use to people might be their tickets to death through their ‘personalized’ airplanes. <br /><br />I hated Daelyn’s character at first. She came across selfish and egotistical. There were times when I wanted to jump in inside the book and strangle her and kill her myself. However, when I scrutinize her character more, I realize it’s not entirely her fault that she turned out who she is. She became the Daelyn that she is because the hurts that she kept vaulted in her heart augmented as she continues to live her life.<br /><br />Santana Lloyd Girard the Second (a renowned lady-killer, or so he says)’s sporadic appearances in Daelyn’s life diluted the abhorrence I once felt for Daelyn. He reminded me of John Green’s The Fault in Our Star’s Augustus Waters. I found him very genteel and nice and funny what with his witty banters and all. I had to cover my mouth to keep myself from totally losing it every time he’d crack a joke.<br /><br />If you have read Jay Asher’s Thirteen Reasons Why and John Green’s The Fault in Our Stars, you might also want to check this book out. It’s a quick-read, fast-paced, and gripping book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16668112195042396671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10018585873254167032" style="display:none">I just finished and closed this book.<br /><br />Typically I would wait to do my review on a book like this. I would sit with it for a few days, but I read this book for a challenge so I'm going to go ahead and write it up. I may change it again later.<br /><br />I struggle with books like these. I'm glad that they are out there - books that deal with REAL issues that kids are having. Not bad hair days, but bad YEARS. days and days and days where they drag on and...when a person reaches a point where they don't feel they can go on.<br /><br />I also don't think these books that deal with real issues - like suicide - should be for adults only. I think it's a very real, very serious issue in our teens, our youth - that dying by their own hand is very much a reality and a choice they choose!<br /><br />But...(you knew that was coming, right?) I know I have my own bias. It's hard for me to read these books and not pull my own stuff in to it. <br /><br />As a mom, I want to scream and yell, scold and...hug and cry and hold her hands and...just crumble because it just breaks my heart that this is an option. That kids die every day by their own hand.<br /><br />As a survivor of all different types of abuse - it always surprises me just how differently we can all handle it. Did I handle it right? Is she handling it wrong? Is it MY place to judge her? Is it her place to judge me?<br /><br />I just...I'm a mom of two girls and a survivor. It's hard not to get angry about a book about suicide - it's hard not to get angry at SUICIDE. It's just hard not to scream and yell and pull this book apart.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=depression">depression</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156586305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6790592434806190639">Sometimes, rarely, a book will have a physical effect on me. Every time that I paused while reading this book, I found myself almost gasping for air. I wasn't exactly holding my breath. It was Daelyn's thoughts that were suffocating me. I can't explain why I felt this way, exactly. Maybe it was the complete sense of emptiness she had. Maybe it was the calm and certain way she was planning her death, after multiple failed attempts. On that note, I feel reading this could be full of triggers for a</span>
  <span id="freeText6790592434806190639" style="display:none">Sometimes, rarely, a book will have a physical effect on me. Every time that I paused while reading this book, I found myself almost gasping for air. I wasn't exactly holding my breath. It was Daelyn's thoughts that were suffocating me. I can't explain why I felt this way, exactly. Maybe it was the complete sense of emptiness she had. Maybe it was the calm and certain way she was planning her death, after multiple failed attempts. On that note, I feel reading this could be full of triggers for anyone, especially teenagers, who have struggled with suicidal thoughts. Read with caution.<br /><br />That's because Daelyn's thoughts and actions feel so real, and so does the bullying she's been subjected to. But nothing everything rings so true. In particular, Santana, the boy who tries to talk to Daelyn, is far too good to be true. I have a hard time believing that he would be that patient about getting her attention. A lot of other details that seemed important to me were left sketchy, far more so than I would have liked. <br /><br />It was an intense read, but there were some issues with the basic plot. I did admire the author for leaving the ending ambiguous, though.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_194717080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194717080" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2069481-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194717080?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2069481-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194717080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5609870171737251205">I absolutely loved this book.<br/><br/>.. until the last page, that is.<br/>While reading this, I, myself, was going through some difficult things as well. Ms. Peters wrote the subject of suicide very, very well. And at times, I actually wanted such a website to exist. There were parts in this book where I yearned to be sitting next to Daelyn, the suicidal, partially mute main character, hugging her, somehow reassuring her things would be okay. And there were parts in this book where I cried, because I related</span>
  <span id="freeText5609870171737251205" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book.<br /><br />.. until the last page, that is.<br />While reading this, I, myself, was going through some difficult things as well. Ms. Peters wrote the subject of suicide very, very well. And at times, I actually wanted such a website to exist. There were parts in this book where I yearned to be sitting next to Daelyn, the suicidal, partially mute main character, hugging her, somehow reassuring her things would be okay. And there were parts in this book where I cried, because I related to so much of Daelyn's thoughts, and how much she wanted to rid herself from this world.<br />With that being said, "By the Time You Read This, I'll Be Dead" was a good read from start to .. well .. almost finish. As much as I loved the book, I hated the sudden ending. I was left wondering with that feeling of wanting to know what happened next. The way Ms. Peters ended this book wasn't with a cliffhanger, but instead with just a sudden ending. It was as if she got tired of writing how much Daelyn wanted to kill herself, and needed a happy ending. However, as much as I detested the ending, I still enjoyed this book, and would read (some parts) it again.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5609870171737251205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_436309725" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436309725" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2121238-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533235366p2/2121238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436309725?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/2121238-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2121238-katherine?shelf=teen-parenting-book-club">teen-parenting-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436309725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3331731660260752664">I read this for the Teen Parenting Program Book Discussion Group. <br/><br/>It is very strange. <br/><br/>I did feel bad for her but she is really being a bummer.<br/><br/>I guess I just wish she could see the good things in life. And I say this coming from a background of being a very depressed teen myself who didn't see the light until after college. But she definitely had some horrible experiences that I can see why she would be acting that way. I guess I just wish I could help her, or that someone had helped her before s</span>
  <span id="freeText3331731660260752664" style="display:none">I read this for the Teen Parenting Program Book Discussion Group. <br /><br />It is very strange. <br /><br />I did feel bad for her but she is really being a bummer.<br /><br />I guess I just wish she could see the good things in life. And I say this coming from a background of being a very depressed teen myself who didn't see the light until after college. But she definitely had some horrible experiences that I can see why she would be acting that way. I guess I just wish I could help her, or that someone had helped her before she got to this point.<br /><br />This book is not as compelling as 13 Reasons Why.<br /><br />The ambiguous ending left me wishing I knew what happened to her after the end of the book. <b>SPOILER ALERT:</b> Even if she had decided to stay alive and fallen in love and all that, since he was sick I just can imagine what would happen when and if he died. And it wouldn't be good. It made me feel like there couldn't really be a happy ending here.<br /><br />Also as a coworker of mine said, it's just too easy. She comes around at the end too fast. I can believe that she had the breakdown with Santana but I don't know if that would have really made her change her philosophy on life so quickly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3331731660260752664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_92685075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92685075" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92685075?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92685075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15263263946425229149">I really liked this book - I would instantly distribute it to a lot of individuals attending my school. Bullying is an abusive, hurtful, and often times overlooked behavior that breaks the self-esteem of kids and teens. It was understandably difficult to read this, but I trudged through the torturous things Daelyn experienced.<br/><br/>Daelyn may be a bit unsympathetic for most readers, but her circumstance made it all the more believable to me. The writing was also solid. I am looking forward to reading </span>
  <span id="freeText15263263946425229149" style="display:none">I really liked this book - I would instantly distribute it to a lot of individuals attending my school. Bullying is an abusive, hurtful, and often times overlooked behavior that breaks the self-esteem of kids and teens. It was understandably difficult to read this, but I trudged through the torturous things Daelyn experienced.<br /><br />Daelyn may be a bit unsympathetic for most readers, but her circumstance made it all the more believable to me. The writing was also solid. I am looking forward to reading more books by Julie Anne Peters - apparently she has a lot of other books published but this was my first from her.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12134788408520434864">Actual rating 4.5<br/><br/>Not a real ''review'' like book bloggers do, but it's something.<br/><br/>I'm not really sure what to say about this book. It was hard for me to read at times, but I never really wanted to put it down. Sometimes I had to, just to give myself time to clear my head. <br/><br/>Daelyn was a very real character, in my opinion. As was Santana. Both characters were different and had their own problems. They complimented each other well. I personally ADORED Santana and his ''relationship'' with Daelyn.<br/><br/>Toug</span>
  <span id="freeText12134788408520434864" style="display:none">Actual rating 4.5<br /><br />Not a real ''review'' like book bloggers do, but it's something.<br /><br />I'm not really sure what to say about this book. It was hard for me to read at times, but I never really wanted to put it down. Sometimes I had to, just to give myself time to clear my head. <br /><br />Daelyn was a very real character, in my opinion. As was Santana. Both characters were different and had their own problems. They complimented each other well. I personally ADORED Santana and his ''relationship'' with Daelyn.<br /><br />Tough subject matter, but definitely an awesome read.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eSy3iby4AacYgxYmVDnD4dznoKim+LDvIXgtYDm0PTKWcjXnaMEoASiXlyvlYPjhJm7isayLZ0xGwaCczs0KEA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vVmhXV5nxxAJi2SvtlKO8IMQzC0GPvR7VKFlRZ5eXZRSByMzih7utjmf5aIHC7XweZmONAxNI9gzGOi5aSdqtg==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_42202024').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_42202024').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_42202024').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16654362276662600142">Julie Anne Peters was born in Jamestown, New York. When she was five, her family moved to the Denver suburbs in Colorado. Her parents divorced when she was in high school. She has three siblings: a brother, John, and two younger sisters, Jeanne and Susan.<br/><br/>Her books for young adults include <i>Define "Normal"</i> (2000), <i>Keeping You a Secret</i> (2003), <i>Luna</i> (2004), <i>Far from Xanadu</i> (2005), <i>Between Mom and Jo</i> (</span>
  <span id="freeText16654362276662600142" style="display:none">Julie Anne Peters was born in Jamestown, New York. When she was five, her family moved to the Denver suburbs in Colorado. Her parents divorced when she was in high school. She has three siblings: a brother, John, and two younger sisters, Jeanne and Susan.<br /><br />Her books for young adults include <i>Define "Normal"</i> (2000), <i>Keeping You a Secret</i> (2003), <i>Luna</i> (2004), <i>Far from Xanadu</i> (2005), <i>Between Mom and Jo</i> (2006), grl2grl (2007), <i>Rage: A Love Story</i> (2009), <i>By the Time You Read This, I'll Be Dead</i> (2010), <i>She Loves Me, She Loves Me Not...</i> (2011), <i>It's Our Prom (So Deal with It)</i> (2012), and <i>Lies My Girlfriend Told Me</i> (2014). Her young adult fiction often feature lesbian characters and address LGBT issues. She has announced that she has retired from writing, and <i>Lies My Girlfriend Told Me</i> will be her last novel. She now works full-time for the Colorado Reading Corps.</span>
